00:31:14","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:14","title":"Dropbox shifts business product focus to remote work with Spaces update","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2075011","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">In a September <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/15/dropbox-ceo-drew-houston-says-the-pandemic-forced-the-company-to-reevaluate-the-product-roadmap/\">interview at TechCrunch Disrupt</a>, <a href=\"http://dropbox.com\">Dropbox</a> co-founder and CEO Drew Houston talked about how the pandemic had forced the company to rethink what work means, and how his company is shifting with the new requirements of a work-from-home world. Today, the company announced broad changes to <a href=\"https://blog.dropbox.com/topics/product/introducing-dropbox-spaces#:~:text=Dropbox%20Spaces%20transforms%20your%20folders,in%20sync%20with%20your%20team.\">Dropbox Spaces</a>, the product introduced last year, to make it a collaboration and project management tool designed with these new requirements in mind.</p>\n<p><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/dropbox\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"dropbox\">Dropbox <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> president Timothy Young says that the company has always been about making it easy to access files wherever you happen to be and whatever device you happen to be on, whether that was in a consumer or business context. As the company has built out its business products over the last several years, that involved sharing content internally or externally. Today&#8217;s announcement is about helping teams plan and execute around the content you create with a strong project focus.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Now what we&#8217;re basically trying to do is really help distributed teams stay organized, collaborate together and keep moving along, but also do so in a really secure way and support IT, administrators and companies with some features around that as well, while staying true to Dropbox principles,&#8221; Young said.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>This involves updating Spaces to be a full-fledged project management tool designed with a distributed workforce in mind. Spaces connects to other tools like your calendar, people directory, project management software &#8212; and of course files. You can create a project, add people and files, then set up a timeline and assign and track tasks, In addition, you can access meetings directly from Spaces and communicate with team members, who can be inside or outside the company.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"SwYOj6cPK3\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/15/dropbox-ceo-drew-houston-says-the-pandemic-forced-the-company-to-reevaluate-the-product-roadmap/\">Dropbox CEO Drew Houston says the pandemic forced the company to reevaluate what work means</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Dropbox CEO Drew Houston says the pandemic forced the company to reevaluate what work means&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/15/dropbox-ceo-drew-houston-says-the-pandemic-forced-the-company-to-reevaluate-the-product-roadmap/embed/#?secret=SwYOj6cPK3\" data-secret=\"SwYOj6cPK3\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Houston suggested a product like this could be coming in his September interview when he said:</p>\n<blockquote><p>“Back in March we started thinking about this, and how [the rapid shift to distributed work] just kind of happened. It wasn’t really designed. What if you did design it? How would you design this experience to be really great? And so starting in March we reoriented our whole product road map around distributed work,” he said.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Along these same lines, Young says the company itself plans to continue to be a remote first company even after the pandemic ends, and will continue to build tools to make it easier to collaborate and share information with that personal experience in mind.</p>\n<p>Today&#8217;s announcement is a step in that direction. Dropbox Spaces has been in private beta and should be available at the beginning of next year.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"uwtyT4rnYi\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/09/29/why-is-dropbox-reinventing-itself/\">Why is Dropbox reinventing itself?</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Why is Dropbox reinventing itself?&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" 00:31:14","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:14","title":"John Legend and Natalie Portman want you to try wearing fungus instead of leather","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2075065","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Natalie Portman and <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/person/john-legend\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"person\" data-entity=\"john-legend\">John Legend <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> are joining a group of venture capitalists and unnamed fashion brands backing <a href=\"https://www.mycoworks.com/\">MycoWorks</a>, a company that just raised $45 million to commercialize its technology that makes a fungal-based biomaterial that can replace leather.</p>\n<p>The goal is to get consumers to trade in their leather and lizard skin couture for some fungus fashion.</p>\n<p>The company said it has inked some deals with big fashion brands as partners as it looks to bring its funky fungus to the masses in shoes, wallets, belts, and other goods that traditionally use cowhide or other animal skins.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>&#8220;We have been working with a few luxury brands and a major footwear manufacturer in very close collaboration,&#8221; said Matt Scullin, the chief executive officer at <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/mycoworks\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"mycoworks\">MycoWorks <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a>.</p>\n<p>The unnamed fashion brands have already started producing products for stores in a range of items including shoes, ready to wear apparel and bags, according to Scullin.</p>\n<p>MycoWorks likes to differentiate itself from other brands that want to bring a fungus among us or plant new plant-based fabrics in fashion &#8212; companies like <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/bolt-threads\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"bolt-threads\">Bolt Threads <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> (mushrooms), Ananas Anam (pineapple fibers), and Desserto (cactus leather) &#8212; with its emphasis on the durability of its fabric.</p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">&#8220;We’ve had the product tested in a huge range of different applications of various leather-based apparel to upholstery to standard leather goods like handbags and wallets. The key difference between our material and mushroom leather is that the structural components is so high,&#8221; Scullin said. &#8220;We&#8217;re confident in the material’s ability to perform in a really wide range of applications so there’s a wide range of uses for that.&#8221;</span></p>\n<p>To that end, MycoWorks is focused on the high-end fo the market. &#8220;<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">There’s a misconception that brands are willing to sacrifice performance for sustainability and that’s not true,&#8221; Scullin said. &#8220;</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The real adoption occurs in an industry like this when the performance is there.&#8221;</span></p>\n<p>Scullin won&#8217;t say how much the MycoWorks material costs nor would he talk about which specific companies are working with the company&#8217;s product right now. He did say that the company hopes eventually to be price competitive with not just the traditional leather market, but the plastic market for leather replacements, which is worth $70 billion per-year alone.</p>\n<p>With the company&#8217;s current capacity it can produce tens of thousands of square feet of fungal material per yar, according to Scullin. That means MycoWorks still has a long way to go to catch up to an industry that produces billions of square feet of leather.</p>\n<p>The funding for MycoWorks is impressive, but it also has to contend with some competitors that are getting traction of their own in the fashion industry.</p>\n<p>In October, Bolt Threads announced the creation of a consortium alongside longtime partners <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/adidas\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"adidas\">Adidas, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> Stella McCartney and the fashion house behind brands like Balenciaga to explore mushroom leather-based products.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"O71u5VbOLl\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/02/bolt-threads-partners-with-adidas-owners-of-balenciaga-and-gucci-and-stella-mccartney-on-mushroom-leather/\">Bolt Threads partners with Adidas, owners of Balenciaga and Gucci, and Stella McCartney on mushroom leather</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Bolt Threads partners with Adidas, owners of Balenciaga and Gucci, and Stella McCartney on mushroom leather&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/02/bolt-threads-partners-with-adidas-owners-of-balenciaga-and-gucci-and-stella-mccartney-on-mushroom-leather/embed/#?secret=O71u5VbOLl\" data-secret=\"O71u5VbOLl\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>For MycoWorks investors including <span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">WTT Investment Ltd. (Taipei, Taiwan), DCVC Bio, </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Valor Equity Partners, Humboldt Fund, Gruss &#38; Co.,</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> Novo Holdings, 8VC, SOSV, AgFunder, Wireframe Ventures, and Tony Faddell, the competition is expected. But they believe that MycoWorks functionality makes it the king (oyster) of the leather substitute world. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&#8220;Fine mycelial leather is customizable to client needs&#8221; said DCVC Bio investor Kiersten Stead. &#8220;[It&#8217;s] customizable in terms of shape, and application. And prices will vary depending on what the application and the criteria from customers is.&#8221;</span></p>\n<p>In all, MycoWorks has raised $62 million and the company&#8217;s new financing announcement coincides with the opening of a new Emeryville, Calif. production plant that takes its capacity up to its current tens-of-thousands of feet of fungal leather replacement capacity.</p>\n<p>Behind all of this push to find replacements for animal skins is a growing awareness of the problems associated with traditional methods for manufacturing leather for clothes and shoes. It&#8217;s a terribly toxic and polluting process, both in the tanning and dyeing and in the waste and landfilling associated with both animal leather and its plastic replacements.</p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&#8220;The process of growing the mycelium is carbon negative. Customers will look at [our product] vs. an animal hide and say why wouldn’t I choose [that],&#8221; said Sculin. &#8220;In addition you have the non-animal aspects and the plastic free aspects that are driving so many decisions right now… what we really are to our brand partners is an advanced manufacturing company. We are motivated by sustainability. We represent a way for them to change their supply chains.&#8221;</span></p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a 00:31:14","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:14","title":"Trust & Will raises $15M as digital estate planning hits mainstream","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2074360","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Let’s get something morbid out of the way right up front: estate planning is a growth business in 2020. Whether you need to create or update a will, build a family trust, or sign over power of attorney for end-of-life decision-making, it’s been a heck of a year for many families, and even more people are starting to think about these instruments if anything worse happens this year (and there are still six weeks left!)</p>\n<p>In the United States, the vast majority of this paperwork is conducted in-person and on paper, but COVID-19 has made that challenging. Digitally native startups are coming to the forefront in this market, just as the market is getting white hot.</p>\n<p>One of the leaders of this pack is <a href=\"https://trustandwill.com\">Trust &#38; Will</a>, which we <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/01/24/trust-will-closes-first-electronic-will-in-the-us-plus-2m-investment/\">first profiled back in early 2019</a>. Two years ago, the startup had just signed the first electronic will in the United States and had raised a $2 million or so seed round led by Rise of the Rest.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Slwp4FtYI2\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/01/24/trust-will-closes-first-electronic-will-in-the-us-plus-2m-investment/\">Trust &#38; Will closes first electronic will in the US (plus $2m investment)</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Trust &#38; Will closes first electronic will in the US (plus $2m investment)&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/01/24/trust-will-closes-first-electronic-will-in-the-us-plus-2m-investment/embed/#?secret=Slwp4FtYI2\" data-secret=\"Slwp4FtYI2\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Now, the startup is returning to the capital trough, picking up a $15 million Series B led by <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/jsv\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"jsv\">Jackson Square Ventures <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> and a bunch of other firms listed below. That brings the company’s total funding to date according to founder and CEO <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/person/cody-barbo\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"person\" data-entity=\"cody-barbo\">Cody Barbo <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> to more than $23 million.</p>\n<p>The company disclosed that it has had 160,000 users sign up for the company’s services since its launch in mid-2018. Trust &#38; Will today has three products: a trust-based estate plan, a will-based estate plan, and “Guardian,” which is a sort of simpler setup for parents with kids. Customers pay an upfront setup fee based on which product they choose, and then they pay a smaller recurring annual subscription fee.</p>\n<p>The company, which originally only worked in Nevada due to the state laws around digital wills, now has attorneys who can assist clients in multiple states. The company has also since conducted the first electronic will in Florida’s history, which, let’s just say, is an important center in the estate-planning industry.</p>\n<p>A couple of other new changes. First, the startup has built up a number of banking and financial planning relationships with institutions such as Fifth Third Bank (which also joined the Series B round as a strategic investor), AARP, and fintech savings startup Acorns.</p>\n<p>Second, the company hired former General Assembly CFO John Zdanowski to take on the startups chief financial officer role. The team has grown to 24, and Barbo noted by email that all three co-founders have become dads since the company’s seed round — putting a bit of a poignant note on their mission to make estate planning accessible to everyone.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2074361\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2074361\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2074361\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/TrustWill_founderbabies.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"454\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/TrustWill_founderbabies.jpg 2100w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/TrustWill_founderbabies.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/TrustWill_founderbabies.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/TrustWill_founderbabies.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/TrustWill_founderbabies.jpg?resize=680,454 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/TrustWill_founderbabies.jpg?resize=1536,1025 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/TrustWill_founderbabies.jpg?resize=2048,1366 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/TrustWill_founderbabies.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2074361\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Trust &#38; Will&#8217;s three co-founders with their very-well-estate-planned children. Photo via Trust &#38; Will.</p></div></p>\n<p>Clearly, the company has a great market tailwind going into 2021, and as more states put in place digital wills and estate planning laws, the market is only set to expand in the coming years. A handful of other startups such as <a href=\"https://www.willful.co\">Willful</a> and the brilliantly-named <a href=\"https://www.freewill.com\">FreeWill</a> are also in this market.</p>\n<p>Today, the company’s board consists of Victor Echevarria from Jackson Square Ventures, Rob Chaplinsky of Link Ventures (which led the company’s Series A), Jesse Draper of Halogen Ventures, Barbo, and Daniel Goldstein, who is co-founder and COO.</p>\n<p>And now, for the long list of all the other investors who participated. In addition to Jackson Square Ventures, new investors for the Series B included Fifth Third Bank, Northwestern Mutual Future Ventures, AARP, Rosecliff Ventures, Hack VC, Actium Partners, Noah Kerner and Jeff Cruttenden. Returning investors included Link Ventures, Rise of the Rest, WTI, Techstars Ventures, Luma Launch, and Halogen Ventures.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a stations","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2074979","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Lunar exploration startup Astrobotic is working on developing ultra-fast wireless charging technology for its CubeRover shoebox-sized lunar robotic explorers. The project, which is funded by NASA&#8217;s Tipping Point program with a $5.8 million award, will tap Seattle-based wireless charging startup WiBotic for expertise in high-speed, short-range wireless power, and brings in Bosch to assist with developing the AI-based data analysis that will help the robots find their way to docking stations for a wireless power-up.</p>\n<p>Existing lunar rovers are typically powered by sunlight, but they&#8217;re actually very large (roughly car-sized or larger) and they have a lot of surface area to soak up rays via solar panels. Astrobotic&#8217;s rovers, which will initially be under five pounds in weight, won&#8217;t have much area to collect the sun&#8217;s power, and will instead have to rely on secondary power sources to keep enough energy for their exploratory operations.</p>\n<p>That&#8217;s where WiBotic comes in. Working together with the <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/university-of-washington\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"university-of-washington\">University of Washington, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> the startup will be developing a &#8220;lightweight, ultra-fast proximity charging solution, compromised of a base station and power receiver&#8221; specifically for use in space-based applications. But finding these stations will be its own special challenge – particularly in a lunar context, where things like GPS don&#8217;t come into play. Instead, Bosch will leverage data collected from sensors on board the robot to generate a sensor-fusion result that can provide it with autonomous navigation capabilities. That work could be instrumental in helping future rovers navigate not only to power stations, but also to various destinations on the lunar surface as robotic science and exploration missions ramp up.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The goal is to have a demonstration rover charging system ready to show off sometime in 2023, and the partners will be working together with NASA&#8217;s Glenn Research Center to test the technology in the facility&#8217;s thermal vacuum chamber test lab.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"OFd6er7Iaf\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/22/cmus-moonranger-robot-rover-will-be-the-first-to-search-for-water-ice-on-the-moon-in-2022/\">CMU&#8217;s MoonRanger robot rover will be the first to search for water ice on the moon in 2022</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/I0vyrzuQpdU\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 17 Nov 2020 14:02:55 +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI","linkMd5":"70bcff6cb5e9328d6343ef926ea37825","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn35@2020_4/2020/11/17/16-31-24-043_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","destWidth":59,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":990,"destBytes":324,"author":"Darrell Etherington","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn35@2020_4/2020/11/17/16-31-24-043_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn56@2020_6/2020/11/17/16-31-36-787_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn38@2020_5/2020/11/17/16-31-34-660_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=I0vyrzuQpdU:VNTU5wcWWQ4:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn76@2020_6/2020/11/17/16-31-34-825_29893022ce85908c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=I0vyrzuQpdU:VNTU5wcWWQ4:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn32@2020_6/2020/11/17/16-31-37-700_738f48174b7347da.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn16@2020_6/2020/11/17/16-31-37-422_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/I0vyrzuQpdU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn35@2020_5/2020/11/17/16-31-36-608_ea76cbe6f8c82a25.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605630674917},{"createdTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:14","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:14","title":"The new Mac mini: The revival of the no-compromise low-cost Mac","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2074668","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">There&#8217;s nothing small about the latest Mac mini.</p>\n<p>Never mind the Mac mini&#8217;s tiny size or low price. This diminutive desktop is a revolution for most users, thanks to <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/apple\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"apple\">Apple&#8217;s <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> new chipset. Called the M1, this chip platform replaces the Intel CPU long found at the heart of Apple&#8217;s desktop and portable computers, and the results are impressive.</p>\n<p>Using the M1 Mac mini feels like using a new iPad or iPhone. Everything satisfyingly snaps into place. I keep waiting for my test machine to start lagging, and nearly a week later, it&#8217;s just as fast as the day I started using it. The new Mac mini is surprising, and most users will find it a major upgrade over existing Mac computers. It&#8217;s hard to beat regardless of the price.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>For casual users, those who live in a web browser or Apple&#8217;s apps, the Mac mini is a no-brainer option. This is the desktop I would buy for myself. Even for power users, those who run bespoke applications, the Mac mini should be seriously considered. Most mainstream applications excel on the new Mini — especially apps with a creative tilt toward photography or video.</p>\n<p>The Mac mini has long been a forgotten friend among the Mac lineup. Hardly updated and never promoted, it sat on the bench for years, watching as Apple&#8217;s portables received updates and refreshes as the world became more mobile. But here we are in the midst of a never-ending pandemic. With coffee shops closed and business travel limited, the COVID-19 crisis could lead to the rediscovery of the desktop computer.</p>\n<p>The M1-powered Mac mini is a winner.</p>\n<h2>Review</h2>\n<p>There are several things you should know. One, the new Mac mini runs the M1 SoC, which is fundamentally different from its Intel predecessor. Instead of a CPU, it&#8217;s an SoC &#8212; System on a Chip, which comes with advantages and concessions. The chipset is built around an ARM design with more integrated components than its CPU counterparts. In many ways, it&#8217;s more similar to the system powering phones and tablets than the chips used in traditional computers. Because of this design, components that used to be discrete are now integrated directly into the chip.</p>\n<p>Second, Apple provided a 6K 32-inch Pro Display XDR with my test Mac mini (these will be returned to Apple). I&#8217;m also running a 24-inch display over HDMI. According to the Mac mini&#8217;s product page, the system is limited to two monitors. I was able to hook up a third monitor through 3rd party software but it was unstable and should not be considered a capability.</p>\n<p>Lastly, you should know TechCrunch also reviewed the new <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/17/macbook-air-m1-review-the-right-apple-silicon-mac-for-most/\">13-inch MacBook Air</a> and <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/17/yeah-apples-m1-macbook-pro-is-powerful-but-its-the-battery-life-that-will-blow-you-away/\">13-inch MacBook Pro</a>. We benchmarked these systems with similar conditions to demonstrate the differences between the units.</p>\n<p>In our tests, we found Apple&#8217;s M1 system on a chip (SoC) to outperform its rivals, regardless of price. With the M1 at its core, the Mac mini is faster in most regards than every Apple computer available except for the ultra-expensive Mac Pro — and sometimes the Mini is faster than the Mac Pro, too. What&#8217;s more, this performance increase is noticeable throughout the system and not just limited to raw computing tasks in purpose-built applications. The system is snappy, responsive and feels like the start of a new era of computing.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"tAi3Cr60KT\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/17/yeah-apples-m1-macbook-pro-is-powerful-but-its-the-battery-life-that-will-blow-you-away/\">Yeah, Apple’s M1 MacBook Pro is powerful, but it’s the battery life that will blow you away</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Yeah, Apple’s M1 MacBook Pro is powerful, but it’s the battery life that will blow you away&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/17/yeah-apples-m1-macbook-pro-is-powerful-but-its-the-battery-life-that-will-blow-you-away/embed/#?secret=tAi3Cr60KT\" data-secret=\"tAi3Cr60KT\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"EgW5RbqdlI\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/17/macbook-air-m1-review-the-right-apple-silicon-mac-for-most/\">MacBook Air M1 review: The right Apple Silicon Mac for most</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;MacBook Air M1 review: The right Apple Silicon Mac for most&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/17/macbook-air-m1-review-the-right-apple-silicon-mac-for-most/embed/#?secret=EgW5RbqdlI\" data-secret=\"EgW5RbqdlI\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<h2>The new Mac experience</h2>\n<p>Snappy hardly describes the experience of the new Mac mini. This system flies. Users will instantly notice the increase in speed, too, from startup time to launching apps. In the past, even on powerful machines, macOS has always felt heavy compared to iOS, but not anymore. With the M1 chip, macOS (Big Sur) is light and free and a joy to use.</p>\n<p>Even better, the ARM-based M1 chip allows Macs to run iOS applications, and they run as smoothly on the Mac as they do on an iPad.</p>\n<p>There&#8217;s likely a hesitation around embracing a new Intel-less Mac. Will your legacy applications run on these machines? Will they run well? I can&#8217;t answer every variable. I installed and ran dozens of applications during my few days with the system and never experienced a roadblock. Even with older programs, everything ran as advertised, and in most cases, ran better on this M1-powered Mac mini than on my few-months-old 15-inch MacBook Pro. I didn&#8217;t find one application unable to run on the new platform.</p>\n<p>The largest speed increases are most noticeable when using native apps for the M1 processor. With Apple&#8217;s Final Cut Pro, the application loads seemingly instantly — two seconds from button press to it being open and ready to go.</p>\n<p>With the M1 chip, it&#8217;s less painful to edit 8K footage in the native Final Cut Pro app than it was to edit 4K footage on an Intel Mac. Exporting the files still takes time, though, and this is one of the few tasks where Intel&#8217;s platform outperforms the M1.</p>\n<p>Even when using legacy software, the system preformed with ease. Edits in Photoshop seemed more fluid. Lightroom loaded photo albums quicker and without hesitation. Editing video in Premiere was easier and less painful as I scrubbed through 6K footage. Even unzipping files was much quicker.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2074937\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2074937\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2074937\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/m1-dock.gif\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"128\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2074937\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Matt Burns</p></div></p>\n<p>This is a silly demonstration, but watch the GIF above. Applications open instantly — all of them at the same time. If Apple put a beachball in this system, I haven&#8217;t found it yet.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-medium wp-image-2074747 alignright\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/chip_cpu__dg71gt6zecya_large_2x.jpg?w=300\" alt=\"\" width=\"300\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/chip_cpu__dg71gt6zecya_large_2x.jpg 984w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/chip_cpu__dg71gt6zecya_large_2x.jpg?resize=150,150 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/chip_cpu__dg71gt6zecya_large_2x.jpg?resize=300,300 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/chip_cpu__dg71gt6zecya_large_2x.jpg?resize=768,768 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/chip_cpu__dg71gt6zecya_large_2x.jpg?resize=680,680 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/chip_cpu__dg71gt6zecya_large_2x.jpg?resize=32,32 32w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/chip_cpu__dg71gt6zecya_large_2x.jpg?resize=50,50 50w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/chip_cpu__dg71gt6zecya_large_2x.jpg?resize=64,64 64w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/chip_cpu__dg71gt6zecya_large_2x.jpg?resize=96,96 96w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/chip_cpu__dg71gt6zecya_large_2x.jpg?resize=128,128 128w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" /></p>\n<p>The M1 chip is based on an ARM design, which required Apple to rework macOS to run on this new computing platform. While it looks mostly the same, the macOS is now purpose-built for Apple&#8217;s own silicon. To take full advantage of the redesigned chip, applications need to be re-coded into an Arm-friendly design. And yet, we found something surprising: Even the apps that are not re-coded yet are still impressively fast thanks to Apple&#8217;s Rosetta 2 that enables software encoded for Intel&#8217;s platform to run on the new Apple platform and take advantage of the M1&#8217;s power.</p>\n<p>For most uses, this holistic approach of building the hardware and software results in major advantages. Common system-level tasks like launching apps, waking from sleep and unzipping files are lightning-fast. Other items like rendering video and editing photos are just as fast, too. Right now, at launch, all of Apple&#8217;s apps &#8212; from Music to Photos to Safari &#8212; are re-encoded for the M1. Like those from Adobe, other apps are not yet native, but the older versions run fine, and in most cases, run better on the M1 than an Intel platform.</p>\n<p>The M1 platform lacks a dedicated graphics processing unit. It&#8217;s built-into the core of the chip. Thanks to a memory dedicated to machine learning, this lack of a discrete GPU is hardly noticeable for professional users. Still, those who do intensive graphics work (like professional gfx visual artists) should hesitate. Even then, this conclusion could change once the applications become native to the new ARM architecture.</p>\n<p>The M1 also lacks the ability to use an eGPU — an external graphics card — but most users should not fret. It could be a problem for pros who found the Intel-based Mac minis paired with a powerful eGPUs as a viable, low-cost alternative to the Mac Pro. However, based on our testing, the GPU performance in these M1 systems are impressive and could be good enough for most, even in creative media editing applications.</p>\n<p>In addition to common workflows, I ran through some industry benchmarks to see how the system responds and came away impressed. We took it one step further, too, and charted the performance between Apple&#8217;s top-of-the-line systems and the new 13-inch MacBook Air and 13-inch MacBook Pro.</p>\n<p>Benchmarks often oversimplify results, but in this case, they seem necessary. This puts systems on common ground. By looking at multiple tests, the results draw a common conclusion. The M1 is really good.</p>\n<h2>The new Mac lineup</h2>\n<p>The Mac mini has two siblings. The M1 is also available in Apple&#8217;s 13-inch MacBook Air and 13-inch MacBook Pro. The differences are minor. The same computing platform powers all three but feature different cooling schemes in the MacBook Pro and Mac mini. Because of the improved cooling, the MacBook Pro and Mac mini are better suited for sustained performance.</p>\n<p>In our testing, all three machines performed similarly. The Air started to fall short in the longer tests, and that&#8217;s likely due to its passive cooling that does not feature a fan. In the MacBook Pro and Mini, the SoC is cooled by a fan, while a heatsink is used in the Air.</p>\n<p>What does this mean for you? For most users, the Air&#8217;s performance is sufficient as it only slows down during long, intensive tasks. For browsing the web, editing photos and watching videos, the Air is perfect.</p>\n<p>There&#8217;s one downside to the new Mac mini over its Intel sibling. The M1 Mac mini only sports two Thunderbolt 3 inputs. For some users, this could be a deal-breaker, though it&#8217;s not for me. There are countless ways to expand the Thunderbolt capability of the Mac mini, and to me, the performance of the machine outweighs the port limitation.</p>\n<p>The M1 Mac mini also lacks a 10GB Ethernet option, limiting its use as a server for some users. This is also likely an M1 limitation, and something I would expect would be addressed in future chipset revisions.</p>\n<p>Multiple monitor support is a major downside to the M1 Mac mini. It only supports two monitors: one through Thunderbolt and one over HDMI. I was able to get a third monitor running at low resolution through third-party software, but it was unstable and performed poorly. To some, including me, multiple monitor support is a major issue and two monitors are often not enough.</p>\n<h2>Benchmarks</h2>\n<p>Apple, when promoting the M1-powered computers, laid out some wild claims about the chipset. We found most of the claims to be factual. We ran a handful of benchmarks on the M1 systems, comparing them against the most recent Macs, including the Mac Pro.</p>\n<p>Benchmarks paint with a broad stroke and often miss nuances. That&#8217;s the case here. While the first few benchmarks demonstrate the speed of the M1, the final test fails to capture a critical aspect of Final Cut Pro. Sure, it&#8217;s slower to export than an Intel-based system, but using the M1-native version of Final Cut Pro is much smoother than what&#8217;s available on older systems. I was able to easily manipulate, scrub and edit 8K footage without even a hiccup. Rendering takes longer, but editing is seemingly easier.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2074941\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2074941\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2074941\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/xcode-unzip-time.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/xcode-unzip-time.jpg 3200w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/xcode-unzip-time.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/xcode-unzip-time.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/xcode-unzip-time.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/xcode-unzip-time.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/xcode-unzip-time.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/xcode-unzip-time.jpg?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/xcode-unzip-time.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2074941\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> TechCrunch</p></div></p>\n<p><strong>Here we downloaded the Xcode 12.3 beta. It&#8217;s an 11.57GB file that extracts a 28.86GB folder. Lower times are better.</strong></p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2074943\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2074943\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2074943\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/webkit-compile-time.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/webkit-compile-time.jpg 3200w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/webkit-compile-time.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/webkit-compile-time.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/webkit-compile-time.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/webkit-compile-time.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/webkit-compile-time.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/webkit-compile-time.jpg?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/webkit-compile-time.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2074943\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> TechCrunch</p></div></p>\n<p><strong>Here we compile WebKit. Lower times are better.</strong></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout aligncenter size-full wp-image-2074944\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/geekbench-intel-rosetta.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2075072\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2075072\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2075072\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/geekbench-arm2.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" using Rosetta 2 to demonstrate the system&#8217;s power when running legacy applications. Then we ran Geekbench in an M1 native mode to test Apple&#8217;s silicon. Higher is better.</strong></p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2074946\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2074946\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2074946\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/final-cut-pro-time.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/final-cut-pro-time.jpg 3200w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/final-cut-pro-time.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/final-cut-pro-time.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/final-cut-pro-time.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/final-cut-pro-time.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/final-cut-pro-time.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/final-cut-pro-time.jpg?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/final-cut-pro-time.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2074946\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> TechCrunch</p></div></p>\n<p><strong>For Final Cut Pro, we timed the rendering of an 8K video (80GB). Lower is better.</strong></p>\n<h2>Conclusion</h2>\n<p><strong>Pros</strong></p>\n<ul>\n<li>Breakthrough performance for the price</li>\n<li>Easily able to run legacy (Intel) and iOS apps</li>\n<li>Cool and quiet</li>\n</ul>\n<p><strong>Cons</strong></p>\n<ul>\n<li>Support for only two monitors</li>\n<li>No eGPU support</li>\n<li>Only two Thunderbolt 3 ports</li>\n</ul>\n<p><strong>Test Mac mini specs</strong></p>\n<ul class=\"as-productsummary-addons\" role=\"list\" aria-label=\"Mac mini\">\n<li class=\"as-productsummary-addon\" role=\"listitem\"><span class=\"\">Apple M1 chip with 8-core CPU and 8-core GPU</span></li>\n<li class=\"as-productsummary-addon\" role=\"listitem\"><span class=\"\">16-core Neural Engine</span></li>\n<li class=\"as-productsummary-addon\" role=\"listitem\"><span class=\"as-productsummary-addonupgrade\">16GB unified memory</span></li>\n<li class=\"as-productsummary-addon\" role=\"listitem\"><span class=\"as-productsummary-addonupgrade\">1TB SSD storage</span></li>\n<li class=\"as-productsummary-addon\" role=\"listitem\"><span class=\"\">Gigabit Ethernet</span></li>\n<li role=\"listitem\">Price as tested: $1,299</li>\n</ul>\n<p>The new Mac mini is a fantastic machine and feels like the start of a quiet revival. In another era, Apple was known for its solid, fairly-priced desktops, which is a great description for this Mac mini.</p>\n<p>As a longtime fan of the Mac mini, I&#8217;m thrilled to see it once again as a great option for those of us who live at a desk .</p>\n<p>With the M1 chipset, Apple is moving onto a new chapter in its long history of personal computers. This chip redefines the computing paradigm by offering stellar performance in a small, power-efficient package. In the Mac mini, the M1 shines as a stable workhorse that provides a new experience to Mac desktops. In the new <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/17/macbook-air-m1-review-the-right-apple-silicon-mac-for-most/\">MacBook Air</a> and MacBook Pro, the M1 is just as solid while offering substantially better battery life than previous offerings. Read those reviews <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/17/macbook-air-m1-review-the-right-apple-silicon-mac-for-most/\">here</a> and here.</p>\n<p>Should you get the new Mac mini? If you&#8217;re stuck at a desk, yes. The new Mac mini is fantastic.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"EgW5RbqdlI\"><p><a 7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn20@2020_2/2020/11/17/16-31-36-680_dfed3e35dad9885a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn16@2020_6/2020/11/17/16-31-37-422_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/adZlG5LAWxg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn52@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-35-737_e8e8495f84021da3.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605630674941},{"createdTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:14","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:14","title":"Microsoft reveals Pluton, a custom security chip built into Intel, AMD, and Qualcomm processors","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2074723","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">For the past two years, some of the world&#8217;s biggest chip makers have battled a series of hardware flaws, like <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/01/03/kernel-panic-what-are-meltdown-and-spectre-the-bugs-affecting-nearly-every-computer-and-device/\">Meltdown and Spectre</a>, which made it possible — though not easy — to pluck passwords and other sensitive secrets directly from their processors. The chip makers <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/03/15/intel-announces-hardware-fixes-for-spectre-and-meltdown-on-upcoming-chips/\">rolled out patches</a>, but required the companies to rethink how they approach chip security.</p>\n<p>Now, <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/microsoft\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"microsoft\">Microsoft <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> thinks it has the answer with its new security chip, which it calls Pluton. The chip, announced today, is the brainchild of a partnership between Microsoft, and chip makers Intel, AMD, and Qualcomm.</p>\n<p>Pluton acts as a hardware root-of-trust, which in simple terms protects a device&#8217;s hardware from tampering, such as from hardware implants or by hackers exploiting flaws in the device&#8217;s low-level firmware. By integrating the chip inside future Intel, AMD, and Qualcomm central processor units, or CPUs, it makes it far more difficult for hackers with physical access to a computer to launch hardware attacks and extract sensitive data, the companies said.</p>\n<p>&#8220;The Microsoft Pluton design will create a much tighter integration between the hardware and the Windows operating system at the CPU that will reduce the available attack surface,&#8221; said David Weston, director of enterprise and operating system security at Microsoft.</p>\n<p>Microsoft said Pluton made its first appearance in the Xbox One back in 2013 to make it far more difficult to hack the console or allow gamers to run pirated games. The chip later graduated to Microsoft&#8217;s cloud service Azure Sphere, used to secure low-cost Internet of Things devices.</p>\n<p>The idea now is to bring that same technology, with some improvements, to new Windows 10 devices.</p>\n<p>The chip comes with immediate benefits, like making hardware attacks against Windows devices far more difficult to succeed. But the chip also solves a major security headache by keeping the device&#8217;s firmware up-to-date.</p>\n<p>Whether or not the Pluton chip can stand the test of time is another matter. Most of the chip vulnerability research has been done by third-party researchers through extensive, and often tedious work. Microsoft&#8217;s Weston said the Pluton chip has undergone a security stress-test by its own internal red team and by external vendors. But that could come back to haunt the company if it got something wrong. Case in point: just last month, security researchers <a href=\"https://www.wired.com/story/apple-t2-chip-unfixable-flaw-jailbreak-mac/\">found an &#8220;unfixable&#8221; security flaw </a>in Apple&#8217;s T2 security chip — a custom-built chip in most modern Macs that&#8217;s <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/10/30/apple-t2-security-chip-microphone-eavesdropping/\">analogous</a> to Microsoft&#8217;s Pluton — that could open up Macs to the very security threats that the chip is supposed to prevent.</p>\n<p>Microsoft declined to say if it planned to offer the Pluton chip designs to other chip makers or if it planned to make the designs open source for anyone to use, but said it plans to share more details in the future, leaving the door open to the possibility.</p>\n<div 00:31:14","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:14","title":"Turo puts $1 million toward helping Black people make money sharing cars","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2074456","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Car sharing marketplace <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/turo\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"turo\">Turo <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> has teamed up with Kiva to offer interest-free loans to Black people and folks from traditionally underserved communities to buy cars and then share them on Turo. The $1 million commitment aims to address the issue of wealth inequality in the United States.</p>\n<p>Called the <a href=\"https://turo.com/us/en/turo-seed-initiative\">Turo Seed Initiative</a>, those who are eligible can raise up to $7,500 via crowdfunding small loans platform. In order to raise money on Kiva, folks must use the funding for business purposes, which includes car-sharing on Turo. Turo will then match whatever the person raises. From there, they can buy a car and list it on Turo.</p>\n<p>&#8220;This will make it easier for people who don&#8217;t have existing assets or the right credit score or doesn&#8217;t own a car to be able to get started that way,&#8221; Turo CEO Andre Haddad told TechCrunch. &#8220;They borrow the money and only reimburse the capital.&#8221;</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Throughout the program, Turo says it will also work with hosts to ensure they can be effective in sharing their cars on Turo. In terms of repayment, Turo has a one-month grace period before hosts must start repaying the funds over a period of 42 months.</p>\n<p>The program is limited to Turo&#8217;s top 15 markets, which include San Francisco, Atlanta, Boston and Houston, in order to ensure that there&#8217;s enough to demand to make it worthwhile for hosts. On average, hosts earn around $600 per month by sharing their vehicles about 11 days per month. On top of that, hosts can also use their cars to drive for Uber or Lyft, or deliver for companies like DoorDash and GrubHub.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We&#8217;re very confident that there is real profit to be made here,&#8221; Haddad said.</p>\n<p>Turo has raised $467.4 million to date and competes against the likes of <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/getaround\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"getaround\">Getaround, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> Car2Go, ZipCar and others. In September, Turo says it saw 17%% year over year growth in revenue and is on track to deliver 20% year over year growth in October. <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/14/getaround-raises-a-140-million-series-e-amid-rebound-in-short-distance-travel/\">In October</a>, Getaround raised a $140 million Series E round to bring its total funding to $600 million. At the time, Getaround said its worldwide revenue had mroe than doubled from its pre-COVID baseline.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a 00:31:14","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:14","title":"Cato Network snags $130M Series E on $1B valuation as cloud wide area networking thrives","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2074949","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a href=\"http://www.catonetworks.com/\">Cato Networks</a> has spent the last five years building a cloud-based wide area network that lets individuals connect to network resources regardless of where they are. When the pandemic hit, and many businesses shifted to work from home, it was the perfect moment for technology like this. Today, the company was rewarded with a $130 million Series E investment on $1 billion valuation.</p>\n<p><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/lightspeed-venture-partners\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"lightspeed-venture-partners\">Lightspeed Venture Partners <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> led the round with participation from new investor Coatue and existing investors Greylock, Aspect Ventures/Acrew Capital, Singtel Innov8 and Shlomo Kramer (who is the co-founder and CEO of the company). The company reports it has now raised $332 million since inception.</p>\n<p>Kramer is a serial entrepreneur. He co-founded Check Point Software, which went public in 1996 and Imperva, which went public in 2011, and was later acquired by private equity firm Thoma Bravo in 2018. He helped launch Cato in 2015. &#8220;In 2015, we identified that the wide area networks (WANs), which is a tens of billions of dollars market, was still built on the same technology stack [&#8230;] that connects physical locations, and appliances that protect physical locations and was primarily sold by the telcos and MSPs for many years,&#8221; Kramer explained.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"OP2yIRkbL5\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/03/31/palo-alto-networks-to-acquire-cloudgenix-for-420m/\">Palo Alto Networks to acquire CloudGenix for $420M</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Palo Alto Networks to acquire CloudGenix for $420M&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/03/31/palo-alto-networks-to-acquire-cloudgenix-for-420m/embed/#?secret=OP2yIRkbL5\" data-secret=\"OP2yIRkbL5\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>The idea with Cato was to take that technology and redesign it for a mobile and cloud world, not one that was built for the previous generation of software that lived in private data centers and was mostly accessed from an office. Today they have a cloud-based network of 60 Points of Presence (PoPs) around the world, giving customers access to networking resources and network security no matter where they happen to be</p>\n<p>The bet they made was a good one because the world has changed, and that became even more pronounced this year when COVID hit and forced many people to work from home. Now suddenly having the ability to sign in from anywhere became more important than ever, and they have been doing well with 2x growth in ARR this year (although he wouldn&#8217;t share specific revenue numbers).</p>\n<p>As a company getting Series E funding, Kramer doesn&#8217;t shy away from the idea of eventually going public, especially since he&#8217;s done it twice before, but neither is he ready to commit any time table. For now, he says the company is growing rapidly, with almost 700 customers &#8212; and that&#8217;s why it decided to take such a large capital influx right now.</p>\n<p>Cato currently has 270 employees with plans to grow to 400 by the end of next year. He says that Cato is a global company with headquarters in Israel where diversity involves religion, but he is trying to build a diverse and inclusive culture regardless of the location.</p>\n<p>&#8220;My feeling is that inclusion needs to happen in the earlier stages of the funnel. I&#8217;m personally involved in these efforts, at the educational sector level, and when students are ready to be recruited by startups, we are already competitive, and if you look at our employee base it&#8217;s very diverse,&#8221; Kramer said.</p>\n<p>With the new funds, he plans to keep building the company and the product. &#8220;There&#8217;s a huge opportunity and we want to move as fast as possible. We are also going to make very big investments on the engineering side to take the solution and go to the next level,&#8221; he said.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote
