+0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI","linkMd5":"c5644e05cc9e2caf1cc83a99954e17c3","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn35@2020_4/2020/11/17/16-31-24-043_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","destWidth":59,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":990,"destBytes":324,"author":"Ron Miller","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn35@2020_4/2020/11/17/16-31-24-043_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn56@2020_6/2020/11/17/16-31-36-787_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn38@2020_5/2020/11/17/16-31-34-660_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=A8d6cPJyHxU:LqrN5z7PVHw:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn59@2020_4/2020/11/17/16-31-34-684_2340454f4ed8f4d7.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=A8d6cPJyHxU:LqrN5z7PVHw:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn96@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-36-043_18d8582221cdcb54.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn16@2020_6/2020/11/17/16-31-37-422_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/A8d6cPJyHxU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn68@2020_4/2020/11/17/16-31-35-774_4d9b6d29ef8ee1aa.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605630674934},{"createdTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:14","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:14","title":"Hover secures $60M for a 3D imaging platform used to assess and fix properties","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2074926","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">The US property market has proven to be more resilient than you might have assumed it would be in the midst of a coronavirus pandemic, and today a startup that&#8217;s built a computer vision tool to help owners assess and fix those properties more easily is announcing a significant round of funding as it sees a surge of growth in usage.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://hover.to/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Hover</a> &#8212; which has built a platform that uses eight basic smartphone photos to patch together a 3D image of your home that can then be used by contractors, insurance companies and others to assess a repair, price out the job, and then order the parts to do the work &#8212; has raised $60 million in new funding.</p>\n<p>The Series D values the company at $490 million post-money, and significantly, it included a number of strategic investors. Three of the biggest insurance companies in the US &#8212; Travelers, State Farm Ventures, and Nationwide &#8212; led the round, with building materials giant Standard Industries, and other unnamed building tech firms, also participating. Past financial backers Menlo Ventures, GV (formerly Google Ventures), and Alsop Louie Partners as well as new backer Guidewire Software were also in this round.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>This funding takes the total raised by Hover to just over $142 million, and for some context on its valuation, it&#8217;s a significant jump compared to its last round, a Series C in 2019, when Hover was valued at $280 million (according to <a href=\"https://my.pitchbook.com/profile/55767-16/company/profile#insights\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">PitchBook data</a>).</p>\n<p>Today&#8217;s funding, that valuation jump, and the interest from insurance firms comes on the heels of huge growth for the company. A.J. Altman, Hover&#8217;s founder and CEO, tells me that in 2016 the startup was making some $1 million in revenues. This year, it&#8217;s expecting to hit &#8220;north of $70 million&#8221; in its annual run rate, with insurance companies and other big business partners accounting for the majority of its growth.</p>\n<p>Hover was founded in 2011 and it first made its name with homeowners and the sole-trader and small business contractors working on their homes repairing roofs and fixing other parts of their structures. Its unique contribution to the market was a piece of software that bypassed a lot of the fragmented and hardest work involved in doing home repair by tying the whole process to the functions of a smartphone: its camera, phone sensors, and the use of apps.</p>\n<p>In essence, it allowed anyone with an ordinary smartphone camera to snap several pictures of a space (up to 8), which could then be used to piece together a &#8220;structured&#8221; 3D image to better assess a job.</p>\n<p>Those 3D images are not ordinary 3D pictures: they are dynamically encoded with information about materials, sizes and dimensions and other data critical to carrying out any work. A contractor using the Hover app could set up a system where these pictures, in turn, could be used to automatically create priced out quotes, with bills of material and timings for work, for their prospective clients. (Compare that to the &#8220;back of the business card&#8221; pricing that typifies quite a lot of jobs, in Altman&#8217;s words.)</p>\n<p>And these days, Hover also serves as an e-commerce portal for builders to order in the parts to carry out that work.</p>\n<p>Hover now has around 35 patents on its tech, Altman said.</p>\n<p>The company has had a lot of traction in the market in part because of how it&#8217;s digitized an analogue process that had before it been firmly offline and lacking in transparency, in what is essentially not just a fragmented process, but also a very fragmented marketplace, with some 100,000 home repair firms active in the US today.</p>\n<p>&#8220;The home improvement segment was one of the few that was not online,&#8221; Altman said. &#8220;For example, if I needed a new roof, it&#8217;s not that easy to just tell me what that would cost. The reason is because someone has to pull dozens of measurements off a house before costing that out, estimating the time it would take to fix and so on. Hover built a pipeline that turns photos into all of those answers.&#8221; It currently has about 10,000 contractors using its app, Altman said, so there is still a lot of growth to go.</p>\n<p>Altman said that in its early days, the company had something of a hurdle convincing people of the usefulness of having an app that let even the homeowner take pictures of an issue on a property in order to start the process of finding someone to fix it. That&#8217;s because even in an age where DIY is pretty commonplace &#8212; and The Home Depot, incidentally, is also a previous backer of Hover &#8212; many builders and their partners see that role as theirs, not their clients.</p>\n<p>That has changed a lot, especially in the last year in the age of a global health pandemic that has driven many to reduce social contacts to help contain the spread of the virus.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Eliminating the need for on-site home visits is a huge deal, but we were spending a lot of time convincing some before Covid that this was a good idea,&#8221; he said. &#8220;The provider &#8212; whether it involved an insurance carrier or contractor &#8212; didn&#8217;t like the idea of engaging a homeowner, asking them, to do that work.&#8221; That has shifted considerably, he said, &#8220;with the Covid experience,&#8221; with many now asking for this option.</p>\n<p>While smaller contractors account for more of its revenues today, insurance is the faster-growing segment of its business, Altman said, where large firms are integrating their apps with Hover&#8217;s, sending out links to customers to snap pictures with the Hover app that then get automatically sent to the insurance company&#8217;s app to kickstart the process of working through customers&#8217; claims.</p>\n<p>“It’s important to us that we provide our customers with the best possible experience, and Hover&#8217;s technology helps us to do that by creating a simpler, faster and more transparent claims process,” said Nick Seminara, executive vice president and chief claims officer of Travelers, in a statement. “We see a tremendous opportunity for Hover in the insurance industry, and we’re pleased to continue our partnership and invest in their future.”</p>\n<p>Longer term, there are a number of areas where you could imagine Hover&#8217;s technology to apply. The company is already doing a lot of work in commercial buildings, and the next step is likely going to be expanding to more interior work, including home design and decor.</p>\n<p>This is a huge market where you could see tech like this linking up with the likes of home sales firms, where companies are able to not just market a home, but potentially fixer-uppers with all the planning work set out for how to fix it up when you buy it; and also of course the extensive landscape of e-commerce businesses selling home furnishings, electronics and more.</p>\n<p>Many of these, like Ikea and Houzz, have already put in a lot of investment into leveraging newer tech like Apple&#8217;s AR platform to improve their user experience, and so the appetite to take things to the next level is definitely there.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=Xw7IDkQHHWY:nS5x45Vy_0M:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=Xw7IDkQHHWY:nS5x45Vy_0M:7Q72WNTAKBA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=Xw7IDkQHHWY:nS5x45Vy_0M:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=Xw7IDkQHHWY:nS5x45Vy_0M:-BTjWOF_DHI\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=Xw7IDkQHHWY:nS5x45Vy_0M:-BTjWOF_DHI\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=Xw7IDkQHHWY:nS5x45Vy_0M:D7DqB2pKExk\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=Xw7IDkQHHWY:nS5x45Vy_0M:D7DqB2pKExk\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=Xw7IDkQHHWY:nS5x45Vy_0M:qj6IDK7rITs\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/Xw7IDkQHHWY\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 17 Nov 2020 14:16:28 +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI","linkMd5":"6956e9d3fb40f912c68f8114b7a0441c","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn35@2020_4/2020/11/17/16-31-24-043_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","destWidth":59,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":990,"destBytes":324,"author":"Ingrid Lunden","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn35@2020_4/2020/11/17/16-31-24-043_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn56@2020_6/2020/11/17/16-31-36-787_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn38@2020_5/2020/11/17/16-31-34-660_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=Xw7IDkQHHWY:nS5x45Vy_0M:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn4@2020_6/2020/11/17/16-31-35-549_e4f909b7a642140b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=Xw7IDkQHHWY:nS5x45Vy_0M:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn89@2020_3/2020/11/17/16-31-49-220_41c229e7e2e832c2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn16@2020_6/2020/11/17/16-31-37-422_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/Xw7IDkQHHWY":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn32@2020_2/2020/11/17/16-31-34-729_f6f1605473baa314.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605630674889},{"createdTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:14","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 00:31:14","title":"MacBook Air M1 review: The right Apple Silicon Mac for most","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2074739","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Reviewing hardware is an act of minutia. Occasionally something new or potentially earth-shattering comes along, but on the whole, it’s about chipping away. Documenting small, gradual changes designed to keep product lines fresh and — if you play your cards right — differentiating yourself from the competition.</p>\n<p><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/apple\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"apple\">Apple’s <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> as guilty of this as anyone, of course. That’s just the nature of a 12 to 24-month product cycle. Every refresh can’t be a revolution. Every so often, however, a game-changer comes along — something undeniable that sets the scene for a more profound shift for a product line. The trio of Macs launched at the company’s third major press conference in three months certainly apply.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"CgTDeGncJ2\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/12/macos-big-sur-is-now-available/\">macOS Big Sur is now available</a></p></blockquote><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;macOS Big Sur is now available&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/12/macos-big-sur-is-now-available/embed/#?secret=CgTDeGncJ2\" data-secret=\"CgTDeGncJ2\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>It’s been 15 years since Apple made the jump to Intel processors from PowerPCs, a chip technology it had relied upon for more than a decade. That move came as the company was butting up against the limitations of its chosen technology. PowerPC took them far at the time, but it couldn’t deliver on the processing power it desired for the next generation of portables.</p>\n<p>As with that transition, the move toward Apple silicon has been years in the making. The company has been making a concerted effort to wean itself off of third-party components. Among other things, it’s increasingly difficult to differentiate your product when you’re essentially using the same parts as everyone else on the market. Creating your own processors is, of course, a long and difficult process. Thankfully, however, the company had a head start.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2074197\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2074197\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2074197\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074517497.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"768\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074517497.jpg 4000w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074517497.jpg?resize=150,113 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074517497.jpg?resize=300,225 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074517497.jpg?resize=768,576 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074517497.jpg?resize=680,510 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074517497.jpg?resize=1536,1152 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074517497.jpg?resize=2048,1536 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074517497.jpg?resize=50,38 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2074197\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Brian Heater</p></div></p>\n<p>The Arm-based chips that power the company’s mobile devices are a great starting point. The company can build on several generations of learning, while moving ever closer to that perpetual Holy Grail of Apple software: perfect cross-ecosystem compatibility. Elements of iOS have been trickling down into MacOS for years now (a trend that includes, and arguably accelerates with, Big Sur), while the company eased the transition for Intel Mac owners with the Catalyst.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2074192\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2074192\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2074192\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074518089.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"768\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074518089.jpg 4000w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074518089.jpg?resize=150,113 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074518089.jpg?resize=300,225 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074518089.jpg?resize=768,576 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074518089.jpg?resize=680,510 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074518089.jpg?resize=1536,1152 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074518089.jpg?resize=2048,1536 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074518089.jpg?resize=50,38 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2074192\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Brian Heater</p></div></p>\n<p>After countless rumors and months of wait, the first three Apple Silicon Macs are finally here. And the results are, in a word, impressive. You’ve no doubt seen some of the benchmarks that have popped up over the past several days that have left many in the community taken aback. While it’s true that Apple talked up performance in its own presser, it’s easy enough to discount those numbers without more specific benchmarks. We’ve split our testing of the three systems among three editors — and it’s pretty safe to say we were blown away by what the systems can do.</p>\n<p>Okay, so, a brief break down of the M1:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Eight-core CPU with a stated 2x performance gain</li>\n<li>Seven- or eight-core GPU (depending on the Air model you go in for) with up to a 2x graphical upgrade</li>\n<li>16-core neural engine</li>\n<li>Increased power</li>\n<li>Improved image signal processing</li>\n</ul>\n<p>The Air, in particular, presents some truly robust gains of the most recent versions of the system, released back in March. That may feel like forever ago, given everything that has transpired, but that’s a mere eight months. The system excels at two benchmarks in particular: battery life — measures by a simple video playback — and Geekbench, which tests a system’s CPU and GPU performance by simulating real-world situations. Anecdotally, things are just faster all over the place.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2074099\" style=\"width: 610px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2074099\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2074099\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/ezgif-1-a7cc1c3ba575.gif\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"516\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2074099\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Brian Heater</p></div></p>\n<p>Apps open almost instantly and resource-intensive tasks like editing 4K video are surprisingly zippy. Some of these are changes you’ll likely notice right away, even if you’re not pushing the system to the limit. Take the neat trick of waking up instantly from sleep. It’s something we’ve taken for granted on mobile devices but haven’t seen as much on desktops.</p>\n<p>These advances, perhaps unsurprisingly, arrive in the same package. Like the new <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/17/the-new-mac-mini-the-revival-of-the-no-compromise-low-cost-mac\">Mac mini</a> and 13-inch Pro, the Air is identical to the one released early this year. Perhaps the company is seeking to maintain consistency on the outside as the products undergo rather dramatic changes under the hood. Maybe a redesign didn’t line up with the move to Arm. Or, hey, maybe Apple thinks the current design represents some sort of platonic ideal for thin and light laptop.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"ddnY7Dp0Qg\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/17/yeah-apples-m1-macbook-pro-is-powerful-but-its-the-battery-life-that-will-blow-you-away/\">Yeah, Apple’s M1 MacBook Pro is powerful, but it’s the battery life that will blow you away</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Yeah, Apple’s M1 MacBook Pro is powerful, but it’s the battery life that will blow you away&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/17/yeah-apples-m1-macbook-pro-is-powerful-but-its-the-battery-life-that-will-blow-you-away/embed/#?secret=ddnY7Dp0Qg\" data-secret=\"ddnY7Dp0Qg\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Whatever the case, you’d be hard-pressed to pick the new Air out of a lineup. I’ve been using the system in public, and no one’s been any the wiser that I got a slight head start on the next generation of Macs. If I’m being honest, I’d have liked it if Apple had ushered the moment in with some befittingly dramatic redesign — but at least no one can accuse Apple of introducing change for the sake of change. And let’s be honest, while the physical design of the Air hasn’t changed much in recent generations, it remains one of the most iconic and better-looking laptops on the market.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"p8bkpxmA0o\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/17/the-new-mac-mini-the-revival-of-the-no-compromise-low-cost-mac/\">The new Mac mini: The revival of the no-compromise low-cost Mac</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;The new Mac mini: The revival of the no-compromise low-cost Mac&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/17/the-new-mac-mini-the-revival-of-the-no-compromise-low-cost-mac/embed/#?secret=p8bkpxmA0o\" data-secret=\"p8bkpxmA0o\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>That includes the same thin and beveled design that differentiates the product from the rest of the MacBook line, and at 2.8 pounds, it’s 0.2 pounds lighter than the 13-inch MacBook. That’s not a huge spread, but it’s something that will make a difference to your lower back over time — I say that as someone who lugged the system around on a 15-mile walk over the weekend.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2074196\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2074196\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2074196\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074517064.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"768\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074517064.jpg 4000w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074517064.jpg?resize=150,113 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074517064.jpg?resize=300,225 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074517064.jpg?resize=768,576 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074517064.jpg?resize=680,510 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074517064.jpg?resize=1536,1152 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074517064.jpg?resize=2048,1536 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074517064.jpg?resize=50,38 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2074196\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Brian Heater</p></div></p>\n<p>Once again, there are two USB-C ports, both positioned on the same side. I’m always going to argue for more ports, especially given the fact that one will semi-regularly be monopolized by a charging cable. I’m also a fan of spreading them out a bit more — preferably on either side of the machine for those instances when you just can’t get enough slack from the cable or have something a bit wider plugged into the port. Of course, there’s no surprise on that front, unlike the new 13-inch Pro, which lost two ports in the process of upgrading.</p>\n<p>That will likely sting for some users attempting to figure out whether to upgrade here. The change appears to be connected to some limitations of the new M1 SOC. If I was a betting man, however, I would suggest that there’s a pretty reasonable possibility that whatever pro-focused version of the chip comes next will support more ports for upcoming devices like the first Apple Silicon 16-inch MacBook Pro.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"QuN0b3wLQO\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/03/20/apple-macbook-air-review/\">Apple MacBook Air review</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Apple MacBook Air review&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/03/20/apple-macbook-air-review/embed/#?secret=QuN0b3wLQO\" data-secret=\"QuN0b3wLQO\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>In fact, the company is likely reserving a number of upgrades to differentiate this round from some new pro-focused devices likely to arrive at some point next year. It’s all part of a kind of configuration of Apple’s Mac strategy that we’re seeing play out in slow motion. The new Air, 13-inch MacBook Pro and Mac mini represent the entry-level tier for the Mac line. It’s a category that’s become an increased focus for the company in recent years — and one we’ve seen play out across the iPhone and Apple Watch lines.</p>\n<p>There is, of course, still truth in the longstanding notion of the premium “Apple Tax,” but the company has expended its approach to improve things on the lower end. One of the more surprising aspects of this strategy on the Mac side is just how much the company has closed the gap between the MacBook Air and 13-inch MacBook. There are differences between the two devices, of course. For many or most, the biggest is the $300 price gulf between the $999 starting price for the Air and $1,299 13-inch MacBook Pro.</p>\n<p>So, how does Apple justify the price difference? And more to the point, will the upsell make a difference for a vast majority of users? Before we go any further, let’s break down the key differences between the new Air and Pro.</p>\n<ul>\n<li><strong>Stated Battery</strong> &#8211; Pro: Up to 20 hours, Air: Up to 18 hours</li>\n<li><strong>Display</strong> &#8211; Pro: 500 nits of brightness, Air: 400 nits</li>\n<li><strong>Microphone Array</strong> &#8211; Pro: Studio-quality three-mic array, Air: Three-mic array</li>\n<li><strong>Touch Bar</strong> &#8211; Pro: Yes, Air: No</li>\n<li><strong>Speakers</strong> &#8211; Pro: Stereo speakers with high dynamic range, Air: Stereo speakers</li>\n<li><strong>Fan</strong> &#8211; Pro: Yes, Air: No</li>\n</ul>\n<p>The last bullet is the most important when it comes to performance. The arrival of the M1 made a fanless MacBook Air a possibility — something that was unheard of in early models. It bodes well for the thinness of future MacBooks, and more immediately, it means extremely silent performance. And, indeed, no matter how much stress testing I’ve managed to do over these past few days, the system has remained eerily silent — though I’d caution you that the passive cooling system can result in a rather toasty Air if you really push things. And, more importantly for a workload standpoint, the system will throttle during resource-intensive tasks — but you’ll have to push it.</p>\n<p>Take, for example, the five-minute, 8K clip we exported in Final Cut Pro. At 33:13 minutes on the Pro and 32:59 minutes on the Air, the end result was, honestly fairly negligible (the Mac Pro, meanwhile, blew them both away at a blazing five and a half minutes). Ditto for running a WebKit compile. That took 25 minutes and five seconds on the Air and 20 minutes and 43 seconds. That’s not entirely negligible, but both systems beat out the 2019 16-inch MacBook Pro’s 26 minutes and 56 seconds. And both systems took far less of a battery hit, losing around 9% during the process, versus the 16-inch’s 39%.</p>\n<p>The new M1 chips are remarkably energy efficient, even when performing more resource-intensive tasks. In a video playback test, I got 16 hours of life. That’s less than the maximum 18 hours stated by Apple’s numbers, but it’s an impressive figure, nonetheless. I would certainly feel comfortable leaving the house without a charge.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout alignnone size-full wp-image-2074098\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-14-at-11.04.20-PM.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"822\" height=\"322\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-14-at-11.04.20-PM.png 822w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-14-at-11.04.20-PM.png?resize=150,59 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-14-at-11.04.20-PM.png?resize=300,118 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-14-at-11.04.20-PM.png?resize=768,301 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-14-at-11.04.20-PM.png?resize=680,266 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-14-at-11.04.20-PM.png?resize=50,20 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 822px) 100vw, 822px\" /></p>\n<p>Per Matthew’s numbers, the Pro fares even better. He was able to get right around the stated 20 hours. That higher figure likely comes due a higher capacity battery courtesy of the thicker laptop footprint. In both cases, however, the systems blew away last year’s 13 and 16-inch Pros, which got eight hours and eight minutes and six hours and 40 minutes, respectively. That’s a tremendous bump in an important metric.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2075072\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2075072\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2075072\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/geekbench-arm2.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/geekbench-arm2.jpg 3200w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/geekbench-arm2.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/geekbench-arm2.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/geekbench-arm2.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/geekbench-arm2.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/geekbench-arm2.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/geekbench-arm2.jpg?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/geekbench-arm2.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2075072\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Bryce Durbin</p></div></p>\n<p>So let&#8217;s break down those Geekbench 5 numbers. The new Air and Pro&#8217;s numbers are quite similar. That&#8217;s to be expected given their respective internals. Again, you&#8217;re going to have to really push the system &#8212; likely for a prolonged amount of time &#8212; before the Air take a noticeable hit due to its fanless design. The Pro scored a 1711 on single core and 7549 on the multi-core. The Air got an average of 1725 and 7563, respectively (for good measure, I&#8217;ll add that the the Mini hit a similar 1748 and 7644).</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout alignnone size-full wp-image-2074944\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/geekbench-intel-rosetta.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/geekbench-intel-rosetta.jpg 3200w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/geekbench-intel-rosetta.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/geekbench-intel-rosetta.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/geekbench-intel-rosetta.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/geekbench-intel-rosetta.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/geekbench-intel-rosetta.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/geekbench-intel-rosetta.jpg?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/geekbench-intel-rosetta.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></p>\n<p>Here&#8217;s some more historical <a href=\"http://So let's break down those Geekbench numbers. The new Air and Pro's numbers are quite similar. That's to be expected given their respective internals. Again, you're going to have to really push the system -- likely for a prolonged amount of time -- before the Air take a noticeable hit due to its fanless design. The Pro scored a 1711 on single core and 7549 on the multi-core. The Air got an average of 1725 and 7563, respectively (for good measure, I'll add that the the Mini hit a similar 1748 and 7644).\">context from Geekbench</a>. A few relevant examples: the Core i7 MacBook Air from earlier this year averaged 1136, while the 13-inch Pro hit 1240. Running the Intel version of the benchmark (using the Rosetta 2 emulator), the numbers predictably took a hit, but still best the Intel systems. And, indeed, Intel-designed apps performed quite smoothly.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2074946\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2074946\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2074946\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/final-cut-pro-time.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/final-cut-pro-time.jpg 3200w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/final-cut-pro-time.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/final-cut-pro-time.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/final-cut-pro-time.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/final-cut-pro-time.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/final-cut-pro-time.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/final-cut-pro-time.jpg?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/final-cut-pro-time.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2074946\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> TechCrunch</p></div></p>\n<p>Most of the benchmarks we ran found the two systems scoring remarkably close to one another. In other words, I think it’s a safe bet a majority of people searching for systems at this tier won’t be bumping up against those kinds of limits too often. Those who do find themselves frequently performing tasks that challenge those hardware limitations are going to have the difficult choice of buying the new 13-inch Pro now or waiting the see what models like the 16-inch have in store. For more information on that front, spend some time with Matthew’s review of the new 13-inch.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2074959\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2074959\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2074959\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-17-at-7.54.32-AM.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"603\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-17-at-7.54.32-AM.png 1990w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-17-at-7.54.32-AM.png?resize=150,88 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-17-at-7.54.32-AM.png?resize=300,177 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-17-at-7.54.32-AM.png?resize=768,452 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-17-at-7.54.32-AM.png?resize=680,400 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-17-at-7.54.32-AM.png?resize=1536,905 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-17-at-7.54.32-AM.png?resize=50,29 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2074959\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Apple</p></div></p>\n<p>What I can say with more certainty, however, is that Apple’s got a much stronger case for its rediscovered focus on creative pros. While the category has long been its bread and butter, a case can be made that the company has surrendered some of that market to the likes of Microsoft’s Surface line and others. Apple made the case that the Touch Bar found it rekindling that relationship, but I think there’s a much stronger case to be made for a MacBook Air that can process much heavier workloads than its predecessors.</p>\n<p>And, frankly, I haven’t missed the Touch Bar. My primary laptop is a 15-inch Pro with Touch Bar, but it’s a feature that hasn’t really impacted my workflow — and it’s not for a lack of trying. I suspect that for those attempting to distinguish between the Pro and Air the missing feature will barely register. And besides, my favorite part of the Touch Bar addition — TouchID — is here as it was on the last Intel version of the Air. On a whole, I’ve found the ability to log in with a fingerprint more useful than scrolling through photos or emojis on the thin touch strip.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2074746\" style=\"width: 610px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2074746\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2074746\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/ezgif-1-93eb04be7f24-1.gif\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"586\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2074746\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Brian Heater</p></div></p>\n<p>Speaking of touch — there’s another elephant in the room here. Obviously the touchscreen Macs some predicted didn’t arrive at the event early this month. Even so, it seems reasonable to expect that they will at some point in the not so distant future, with the lines continuing to blur between macOS and iOS. Look no further than Big Sur, which continues the recent trend of adopting key features from the mobile operating system.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2074664\" style=\"width: 610px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2074664\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2074664\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/ezgif-7-4b3d456ba000.gif\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"466\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2074664\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Brian Heater</p></div></p>\n<p>As I noted in my recent writeup of macOS 11.0, a number of features are practically begging for touchscreen interaction. Take the sliders in the newly added Control Center. Sure, the trackpad works fine, but it sure would be satisfying to swipe them over with a finger. This becomes even more pronounced when playing certain iOS optimized games, which now play natively on the M1. Take &#8220;Among Us.&#8221; I played the wildly popular social game on the new Air — and while the gameplay was predictably smooth, playing with the trackpad feels less natural than touch.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"CgTDeGncJ2\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/12/macos-big-sur-is-now-available/\">macOS Big Sur is now available</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;macOS Big Sur is now available&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/12/macos-big-sur-is-now-available/embed/#?secret=CgTDeGncJ2\" data-secret=\"CgTDeGncJ2\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>In this implementation, you either have to use the pointer to control an on-screen joypad or simply point the character in the right direction. There’s also the fact that the game occupies a fixed window that you can’t expand to take up the full display. The M1 chip goes a long ways toward opening up the available Mac ecosystem, making porting an iOS app as simple as ticking a box to make it available through the Mac App Store, but in many cases, additional optimization for these systems is warranted particularly for more professionally minded applications.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2074194\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2074194\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2074194\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074519411.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"768\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074519411.jpg 4000w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074519411.jpg?resize=150,113 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074519411.jpg?resize=300,225 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074519411.jpg?resize=768,576 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074519411.jpg?resize=680,510 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074519411.jpg?resize=1536,1152 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074519411.jpg?resize=2048,1536 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074519411.jpg?resize=50,38 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2074194\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Brian Heater</p></div></p>\n<p>As for the other primary input device, the keyboard is pretty much the same as the latest Intel Air — which is to say head and shoulders above early versions. That’s no doubt a dark couple of generations of keyboards Apple would like to forget. They were solid as a rock, and insufferably loud. They also caused a lot of users undue stress by getting jammed. The latest version of the scissor mechanisms are far superior to the early butterflies. I won’t go so far as saying it’s the best laptop typing experience, but it’s like night and day compared to early models.</p>\n<p>Another aspect that warrants mention is the webcam. It’s a feature that rarely warrants a sentence in most laptop reviews, but this is 2020. It’s a weird year with weird demands and here we are carrying out the vast majority of our interaction with other human beings over Zoom. It sucks, but it’s life. Many people have no doubt already invested in external webcams as part of the shift toward working from home. For the first time in — well, probably ever — webcams are an important factor in purchasing for many or even most people.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2074094\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2074094\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2074094\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Photo-on-11-15-20-at-11.35-AM-1.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"365\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Photo-on-11-15-20-at-11.35-AM-1.jpg 2020w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Photo-on-11-15-20-at-11.35-AM-1.jpg?resize=150,53 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Photo-on-11-15-20-at-11.35-AM-1.jpg?resize=300,107 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Photo-on-11-15-20-at-11.35-AM-1.jpg?resize=768,274 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Photo-on-11-15-20-at-11.35-AM-1.jpg?resize=680,242 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Photo-on-11-15-20-at-11.35-AM-1.jpg?resize=1536,547 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Photo-on-11-15-20-at-11.35-AM-1.jpg?resize=50,18 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2074094\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Brian Heater</p></div></p>\n<p>Apple has, indeed, upgraded the camera for the latest Air — but not entirely. That is to say the sensor is the same, and the camera is still stuck at 720p. But the new image signal processor (ISP) included as part of the M1’s SOC design does result in a better image. You can see the difference above. Frankly, neither is great to be honest, but one is decidedly less bad than the other. On the left you’ll see the Air’s image.</p>\n<p>The resolution is still low, but the color — among others — is certainly improved. The white balance is more inline with reality and it handles shades better. I’m going to still defer to my external webcam for things like Extra Crunch panels, but for a quick meeting, sure, I’m fine letting the Air do the job. This would have been a perfect time for Apple to go all-in with a webcam refresh on these systems. Common wisdom says there are limitations on camera hardware give the thickness of the laptop lid, but if I had to venture a guess here, I’d say the company is looking at webcam video as another point of differentiation for Pro models.</p>\n<p><!--[if lt IE 9]><script>document.createElement('audio');</script><![endif]-->\n<audio class=\"wp-audio-shortcode\" id=\"audio-2074739-1\" preload=\"none\" style=\"width: 100%;\" controls=\"controls\"><source type=\"audio/wav\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/macbook-air-audio.wav?_=1\" /><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/macbook-air-audio.wav\">https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/macbook-air-audio.wav</a></audio></p>\n<p>The microphone, meanwhile, remains a point of distinction between the Air and Pro. I’ve included voice recordings from the Intel and Arm Airs above. See if you can tell the difference. Honestly, I can’t, really. As with the webcam, they’re fine for a casual chat, but I wouldn’t want to, say, record a podcast on the thing.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout alignnone size-full wp-image-2074984\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/4k60-Full-Screen-Video-Playback.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"630\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/4k60-Full-Screen-Video-Playback.png 1876w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/4k60-Full-Screen-Video-Playback.png?resize=150,92 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/4k60-Full-Screen-Video-Playback.png?resize=300,185 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/4k60-Full-Screen-Video-Playback.png?resize=768,472 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/4k60-Full-Screen-Video-Playback.png?resize=680,418 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/4k60-Full-Screen-Video-Playback.png?resize=1536,945 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/4k60-Full-Screen-Video-Playback.png?resize=50,31 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></p>\n<p>These three new systems represent the first step toward Mac’s future. And there’s a lot to be excited about when it comes to the potential of Apple Silicon. The M1 chip already displays some pretty dramatic performance gains for a lot of tasks, coupled with substantial increases in battery life, courtesy of decreased power consumption.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2074191\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2074191\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2074191\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074419281.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"768\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074419281.jpg 4000w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074419281.jpg?resize=150,113 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074419281.jpg?resize=300,225 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074419281.jpg?resize=768,576 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074419281.jpg?resize=680,510 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074419281.jpg?resize=1536,1152 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074419281.jpg?resize=2048,1536 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/2020-11-16-074419281.jpg?resize=50,38 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2074191\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Brian Heater</p></div></p>\n<p>There are some limitations worth noting on these models. Two USB-C ports appears to be the maximum in the current configuration and all three models currently top out at 16GB of RAM. If either of those are dealbreakers, the company will happily still sell you an Intel model for the foreseeable future.</p>\n<p>When Apple Silicon was announced at WWDC back in June, Tim Cook noted that it would take two years to transition the full line. That means we’re very much at the beginning of this journey and there’s a lot left to reveal, including how dramatically different the true Pro tier of MacBooks look.</p>\n<p>For most users with most needs, the Air is a fine choice. If I had to buy a new MacBook today I would pull the trigger on Air and upgrade the memory and storage for good measure. It’s a surprisingly powerful machine in a compact package.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"MNt8ME7MEC\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/10/heres-everything-apple-announced-at-the-one-more-thing-event-today/\">Here&#8217;s everything Apple announced at the &#8216;One More Thing&#8217; event today</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Here&#8217;s everything Apple announced at the &#8216;One More
